Comment

This whole prose hymn is found in P─Бipp. xvi., except a few verses, as noted below. It is not quoted by either K─Бu┼Ы. or V─Бit. In the Pr─Бt., on the other hand, it has more than its fair share of notice. тМКWith regard to the pary─Бya-hymns in general, see pp. 471-2.тМЛ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╢реВрд░реНрдкрдореН) рд╕реВрдк [рдЫрд╛рдЬ], (рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░рдореН) рдЪрд╛рд▓рдиреА, (рддреБрд╖рд╛рдГ) рдмреБрд╕реА (рдЛрдЬреАрд╖рд╛) рд╕реЛрдо рдХрд╛ рдлреЛрдХ [рдиреАрд░рд╕ рд╡рд╕реНрддреБ], (рдЕрднрд┐рд╕рд╡рдиреАрдГ) рдорд╛рд░реНрдЬрди рд╡рд╛ рд╕реНрдирд╛рди рдХреЗ рдкрд╛рддреНрд░, (рдЖрдкрдГ) [рдпрдЬреНрдЮ рдХрд╛] рдЬрд▓ред (рд╕реНрд░реБрдХреН) рд╕реНрд░реБрдЪрд╛ [рдШреА рдЪреЭрд╛рдиреЗ рдХрд╛ рдкрд╛рддреНрд░], (рджрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдГ) рдЪрдордЪрд╛, (рдиреЗрдХреНрд╖рдгрдореН) рд╢реВрд▓, рд╢рд▓рд╛рдХрд╛ рдЖрджрд┐, (рдЖрдпрд╡рдирдореН) рдХрдврд╝рд╛рд╣реА, (рджреНрд░реЛрдгрдХрд▓рд╢рд╛рдГ) рджреНрд░реЛрдгрдХрд▓рд╢ [рдпрдЬреНрдЮ рдХреЗ рдХрд▓рд╢], (рдХреБрдореНрднреНрдпрдГ) рдХреБрдореНрднреА [рдЧрд░реНрдЧрд░реА], (рд╡рд╛рдпрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐) рдкрд╡рди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдХреЗ (рдкрд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐) рдкрд╛рддреНрд░ [рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╣реИрдВ], (рдЗрдпрдореН) рдпрд╣ [рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА] (рдПрд╡) рд╣реА [рд╕рдВрдиреНрдпрд╛рд╕рд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ] (рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╛рдЬрд┐рдирдореН) рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╕рд╛рд░ рд╣рд░рд┐рди рдХреА рдореГрдЧрдЫрд╛рд▓рд╛ [рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рд╣реИ] реерезрем, резренрее

Whitney
Translation
  1. The spoon is the sacrificial spoon, the stirring-stick the spit (?
    n├йkс╣гaс╣Зa), the kettles the wooden vessels, the drinking-vessels those
    of V─Бyu, this [earth] itself the black antelope’s skin.
Notes

Ppp. reads -kala┼Ыaс╣г kumbh─лm eva kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З─Бjinaс╣Б v─Бyavy─Бni p─Бtr─Бс╣Зi; and it
also has abhiс╣гavaс╣З─лr ─Бpaс╕е in this verse, after ─Бyavanam, instead of
in vs. 16. The Anukr. defines the verse as if it were metrical, and
intends us to read it as 10 + 16 + 8 = 34 syllables.

triс╣гс╣нubh; 20. ─Бsury anuс╣гс╣нubh; 21. s─Бmny uс╣гс╣Зih; 22, 28. s─Бmn─л bс╣Ыhat─л (28.
bhurij); 23. ─Бrcy anuс╣гс╣нubh; 24. 3-p. svar─Бс╕Н anuс╣гс╣нubh;* 25. ─Бsur─л
g─Бyatr─л;тАа 26. s─Бmny anuс╣гс╣нubh; 27. 3-p. ─Бrc─л triс╣гс╣нubh; 30. 3-p. ─Бrc─л
pan╠Дkti.] *тМКBerlin ms.: 3-p. vir─Бс╣н purast─Бdbс╣Ыhat─л.тМЛ тАатМКBerlin ms.:
s─Бmny anuс╣гс╣нubh.тМЛ

Griffith

Spoon, ladle, fork, stirring-prong are the wooden Soma tubs; the earthen cooking-pots are the mortar-shaped Soma vessels; this earth is just the black-antelope’s skin.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The lord of guests verily makes for himself a sacrificer’s
    br─Б╠Бhmaс╣Зa in that he looks at the [portions] to be partaken of,
    saying “is this larger, or this?”
Notes

Several of the mss. (O.R.D.) accent at the end bh┼л╠Бy─Б╠Бs (D. bh┼л╠Бy─Б╠Бс╕е 3),
which is the far preferable reading; bh┼л╠Бy─Бs (read by I.) could be
borne, since in RV. and AV. the usage does not seem yet established that
the protracted final syllable is acute, in addition to whatever accent
the word may have on other syllables тМКSkt. Gram. ┬з78тМЛ; but bh┼лy─Бs,
as our edition reads, in accordance with nearly all the mss. compared up
to the time of its publication, is nothing but a blunder. The protracted
words are quoted in Pr─Бt. i. 105. The verse counts naturally 18 + 8 + 8
= 34 syllables (the second and third p─Бdas being really metrical). тМКScan
rather 10 + 8 + 8 + 8 with the Anukr.тМЛ Ppp. reads kс╣Ыс╣Зute and
avekс╣гata.

Griffith

Or the host acts in this way to a Yajamana’s Brahman: when he looks at the furniture and utensils he says, More here t yet more here.

before our vs. 49 тМКand without variant except c─Бrtvijas, which may be

Griffith

Now these guests, as priests beloved or not beloved, bring one to the world of Svarga.

реирек рд╕ рдп ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. He who, knowing thus, shall partake, not hating, he shall not
    partake the food of one hating, not of one that is doubted, nor of one
    doubting (?).
Notes

We must emend at the end either to m─л╠Бm─Бс╣Еsam─Бnasya or to
m─лm─Бс╣Еsy├бm─Бnasya; the translation assumes the former. Bp.┬╣ reads
vidy─Б╠Бt for vidv─Б╠Бn, and it would be a welcome improvement; the same
reads the first time a┼Ыn─лy─Б╠Бt, which seems necessary if vidv─Б╠Бn and
not vidy─Б╠Бt is read, and which is implied in the translation. Ppp. has
instead tasm─Бn na dviс╣гann ady─Бn na dviс╣гato тАШnnam ady─Бn na m─лm-. The
two mss. of the Anukr. describe the verse differently but equivalently,
both requiring 34 syllables (which implies restoration of тАШnnam to
├бnnam).

Griffith

He who hath this knowledge should not eat hating, should not eat the food of one who hates him, nor of one who is doubt- ful, nor of one who is undecided.

well as 26 a s─Бmny anuс╣гс╣нubh тМК16 syllablesтМЛ. тМКVss. 25 and 26 have each

Whitney
Translation
  1. [The fire] that is the guests’, that is the fire of libations
    (─Бhavan─л╠Бya); the one in the dwelling (v├й┼Ыman), that is the
    householder’s fire (g─Б╠Бrhapatya); the one in which they cook, that is
    the southern fire (dakс╣гiс╣З─Бgn├н).
Notes

Ppp. reads s─Б тАЭhavan─лyo yo тАШnnakaraс╣Зasya тМКintending -karaс╣Зas sa?тМЛ
dakс╣гiс╣З─Бgnir yo ve┼Ы- sa g─Бr-. The metrical definition of the Anukr.
requires us to restore at the beginning y├│ ├бtith-.

[Pary─Бya III.тАФnavakaс╕е. 31-36, 39. 3-p. pip─лlikamadhy─Б g─Бyatr─л;
37. s─Бmn─л bс╣Ыhat─л; 38. pip─лlikatnadhyo тАЩс╣гс╣Зih.]

Griffith

The fire of the guests is the Ahavaniya, the fire in the dwelling is the Garhapatya, that whereon they cook food is the South- ern Sacrificial Fire.

Translation
  1. Verily both what is sacrificed and what is bestowed of the houses
    doth he partake of who partakes before a guest.
Notes

That is, doubtless, ‘doth he eat up, devour, destroy.’ Ppp. omits
gс╣Ыh─Бс╣З─Бm, and puts next vss. 34 and 33, omitting 35 and 39 тМКand 32 and
36 alsoтМЛ. The Anukr. describes the paragraphs as if they were metrical,
and defines them as if the text read p┼л╠Бrvo ├бtither.

Griffith

Now that man who eats before the guest eats up the sacrifice and the merit of the house.

Whitney
Translation
  1. He verily is a guest, namely (y├бt) one versed in sacred learning
    (┼Ыr├│triya); before him one should not partake.
Notes

The meaning intended ought to be that a guest is the equivalent of such
a sage; but the literal sense is as translated. The verse lacks one
syllable (unless we read n├б a┼Ыn─лy─Бt) of being full measure.

Griffith

The man should not eat before the guest who is a Brahman versed in holy lore.

Translation
  1. When the guest hath partaken he should partake, in order to the
    soulfulness of the sacrifice, in order to the integrity of the
    sacrifice; that is the [proper] course.
Notes

The verse is an uс╣гс╣Зih only as containing (if we resolve a┼Ыit─Б╠Бvati
├бt-) 28 syllables (11 + 14 + 3). The pada-text reads a┼Ы─лt├бре░vati.
Ppp. has a┼Ыit─Бvaty a┼Ыn─лy─Бt tad vrataс╣Б yaj├▒asy─Б тАЩviched─Бya yaj├▒asya
guptaye yaj├▒asya s─Бtmatv─Бya. тМКCf. Oldenberg, IFA. vi. 184: also Skt.
Gram. ┬з960.тМЛ

Griffith

When the guest hath eaten he should eat. This is the rule for the animation of the sacrifice and the preservation of its continuity.

Whitney
Translation
  1. That verily is specially sweet which comes from the cow
    (adhigav├б), either milk (kс╣г─лr├б) or flesh; that he should not partake
    of.
Notes

That is, doubtless, he should leave it for his guest. The verse is
wanting in Ppp. The so-called g─Бyatr─л is to be thus divided: 7 + 11 +
6 = 24.

[Pary─Бya IV.тАФda┼Ыakaс╕е. a of 40-43. pr─Бj─Бpaty─Б тАЩnuс╣гс╣нubh;
a of 44. bhurij; b of 40-43. 3-p . g─Бyatr─л; b of 44.
4-p. prast─Бrapan╠Дkti.]

Griffith

Now the sweetest portion, the produce of the cow, milk, or flesh, that verily he should not eat.

рекреж рд╕ рдп ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. He who, thus knowing, pouring out milk, presents [it]тАФas much as,
    having sacrificed with a very successful agniс╣гс╣нom├б, one gets
    possession of, of so much thereby does he get possession.
Notes

The mss. are divided between reckoning ten verses (with the Anukr. тМКcf.
the quotations etc. at the end of the hymnтМЛ) in this section, or only
five, with two parts to each; the latter method was adopted in our
edition as the better. The second part in the first five verses, though
doubtless meant only as prose, divides into three subdivisions of eight
syllables each, like a real g─Бyatr─л. Ppp. begins all the verses with
yat, instead of sa ya evaс╣Б vidv─Бn, and reads in 40 b y─Б. ag.
sapс╣Ыс╣гс╣нhene тАЩс╣гс╣нv─Б тАЩvarundhe.

Griffith

The man who having this knowledge pours out milk and offers it wins for himself as much thereby as he gains by the perfor- mance of a very successful Agnishtoma sacrifice.

Translation
  1. He who, thus knowing, pouring out butter (sarp├нs), presents
    [it]тАФas much as, having sacrificed with a very successful atir─Бtr├б,

Whitney
Translation
  1. He who, thus knowing, pouring out meat, presents [it]тАФas much as,
    having sacrificed with a very successful twelve-day sacrifice, one gets
    etc. etc.
Notes
Griffith

He who having this knowledge besprinkles flesh and offers it wins for himself thereby as much as he gains by the perfor- mance of a very successful Twelve-Day sacrifice.

Griffith

The man who having this knowledge pours out water and offers it obtains a resting-place for the procreation of living beings and becomes dear to living beings, even the man who having this knowledge pours out water and offers it.

Whitney
Translation
  1. For him the dawn utters hing; Savitar preludes (pra-stu);
    Brihaspati with refreshment (┼лrj├бy─Б) sings the udg─лth├б; Tvashс╣нar
    with prosperity responds (prati-hс╣Ы); all the gods [are] the
    conclusion (nidh├бna); the conclusion of thrift, of progeny, of cattle
    becometh he who knoweth thus.
Notes

Here and in the following verses тМКcf. PB. iv. 9. 9тМЛ are had in view the
five successive parts or divisions of a s─Бman, of which the udg─лtha
is the central and principal: cf. Ch─Бnd. Upan. ii. 2 ff. In this section
also the majority of the mss. divide and number in accordance with our
edition; the rest, with the Anukr., number the subdivisions
successively. Our edition assumes the subdivision nidh├бnam bh┼л╠Бty─Бс╕е to
be repeated at the end of each of the four paragraphs; the Anukr.
тМКcounting 10 (not 12) avas─Бnarcas: cf. p. 546 belowтМЛ is against this;
as for the mss., their testimony is nothing, since they all, in any
case, write such an addition only the first time and the last, omitting
all intermediate occurrences; it is altogether probable that the edition
is right. The artificial description by the Anukr. of b as an
uс╣гс╣Зih, implies resolving ┼лrj├бy─Б ├║d, and either p├║с╣гс╣нi-─Б or
v├н┼Ыu-e. Ppp. adds v─Бi after tasm─Бi, and bh┼лty─Б after savit─Б,
and reads ┼лrj─Б for ┼лrjay─Б.

Griffith

For him Dawn murmurs, and Savitar sings the prelude; Brihas- pati chants with vigour, and Tvashtar joins in with increase; the Visve Devah take up conclusion. He who hath this know- ledge is the abiding-place of welfare, of progeny, and of cattle.

Whitney
Translation
  1. For him the rising sun utters hing; cow-gathering time (saс╣Бgav├б)
    preludes; noon sings the udg─лth├б; afternoon responds; the setting
    [sun is] the conclusion: the conclusion of etc. etc.
Notes

Ppp. combines madhyandino тАЩd. The тМКnicс╣ЫtтМЛ “dissimilar g─Бyatr─л,”
b, divides as 8 + 9 + 6 = 23.

Griffith

For him the rising Sun murmurs, and Early Morning sings the prelude; Noon chants the psalm, Afternoon joins in; the setting Sun takes up the conclusion. He who hath this know- ledge is the abiding place of welfare, of progeny, and of cattle.

Whitney
Translation
  1. For him the cloud, forming (bh┼л), utters hing; thundering, it
    preludes; lightenng, it responds; raining, it sings the udg─лth├б;
    holding up, it is the conclusion: the conclusion of etc. etc.
Notes

Ppp. reads vidyotam─Бnaс╕е pra st─Бuti stanayann ud g─Бyati apar─Бhс╣Зa prati
harati astaс╣Бyaс╣Б nidhanam. The “dissimilar g─Бyatr─л,” b, is this
time 10 + 6 + 6 = 22. Bp.Bp.┬▓p.m.D. read v├бrс╣гam, and several of the
saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. varс╣гaс╣Бn instead of -с╣гann. Cf. Ch─Бnd. Upan. ii. 3.

Griffith

For him the Rain-cloud murmurs when present, sings the pre- lude when thundering, joins in when lightening, chants the psalm when raining, and takes up the conclusion when it stays the downpour. He who hath this knowledge is the abiding- place of welfare, of progeny, and of cattle.

Whitney
Translation
  1. [When] he meets the guests with his eyes, he utters hing;
    [when] he greets [them], he preludes; [when] he offers water, he
    sings the udg─лth├б; [when] he presents [food], he responds; the
    remnant (├║chiс╣гс╣нa) [of the food] is the conclusion: the conclusion of
    etc. etc.
Notes

Ppp. seems again to mix in matter from vs. 46, reading y─Бcaty udakavaty
apar─Бhс╣Зa* prati harati. тМКSee also note to vs. 23.тМЛ The first
subdivision makes the 30 syllables required by the Anukr. if we give
syllabic value (-ti) to the thrice-occuring verb-ending -ty; and
similarly we get 16 for b. *тМКThe phonetic resemblance of
udakavati to ud g─Бyati (cf. note to ii. 13. 3) and of apar─Бhс╣Зa to
upa harati is obviously the occasion for the confusion.тМЛ

[Pary─Бya VI.тАФcaturda┼Ыakaс╕е. 49. ─Бsur─л g─Бyatr─л; 50. s─Бmny anuс╣гс╣нubh;
51, 53. 3-p. ─Бrc─л pan╠Дkti; 52. 1-p. pr─Бj─Бpaty─Б g─Бyatr─л; 54-59. ─Бrc─л
bс╣Ыhat─л; 60. 1-p. ─Бsur─л jagat─л; 61. y─Бjuс╣г─л triс╣гс╣нubh; 62. 1-p. ─Бsury
uс╣гс╣Зih.]

Griffith

He looks at the guests, he utters a gentle sound; he speaks, he signs the prelude; he calls for water, he chants the psalm; he offers the residue of the sacrifice, he takes up the conclusion.

Whitney
Translation
  1. He тМКthe guest?тМЛ, being invited (├║pah┼лta), feeds (bhakс╣гay-) on
    the earth; in him тМКlocativeтМЛ, invited тМКnominativeтМЛ, [he тМКthe host?тМЛ
    feeds on] what of every form [there is] on the earth.
Notes

тМКWhitney’s first “on” is intended as a rendering of the locative
relation of “earth”; his second “on” goes with “feeds.” He has tried to
indicate this by putting the first after the parenthesis and the second
within the brackets. The inherent ambiguity of the English combination
is such that I do not know how to remove it for the non-Sanskritist save
by an express statement.тМЛ

The sense of this and the following verses is very obscure; it is here
translated as if the guest were the subject of the first bhakс╣гayati,
and the entertainer (in recompense for the entertainment given) of the
second тМКbhakс╣гayati (supplied)тМЛ. Ppp. adds pс╣Ыthivy─Бс╣Б tat pс╣Ыthivy─Бm ─Б
bh─Бti svargo loko bhavati ya evaс╣Б veda. Only vs. 56 has the full number
of syllables (27) belonging to an ─Бrc─л bс╣Ыhat─л; 55, 58, 59 have only 26
syllables (a number for which the system affords no separate name), and
57 has only 24.

Griffith

He having been invited on earth, regales, invited in that, which wears all various forms on earth.
